href=\"http:\/\/bit.ly\/2nu8CAX\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">break it down<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> on the dance floor with former South African president Jacob Zuma? And are enterprising South African criminals using <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/africacheck.org\/reports\/are-spiked-oranges-the-latest-hijacking-ploy-in-south-africa\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">nail-spiked oranges<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> to hijack motorists?<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Africa Check senior researcher, Kate Wilkinson, busted these hoaxes when she spoke to Power FM\u2019s Iman Rappetti on Thursday about how to <\/span><a href=\"http:\/\/bit.ly\/2nu8CAX\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">fact-check viral images<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">During the discussion, a listener <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/HesedGuru\/status\/969149522072014849\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">tweeted us an image<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> for our closer inspection.<\/span><\/p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet tw-align-center\" data-lang=\"en\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\" lang=\"en\"><a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/imanrappetti?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@imanrappetti<\/a> Can <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/AfricaCheck?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@AfricaCheck<\/a> verify this lie too, I once sow on Pepsi one now this. Problem is, same guy, same police, same place but different reasons <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Powerfm987?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@Powerfm987<\/a> <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/ugNw68uf3J\">pic.twitter.com\/ugNw68uf3J<\/a><\/p>\n<p>\u2014 Cyprian from Brits (@HesedGuru) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/HesedGuru\/status\/969149522072014849?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 1, 2018<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cCan @AfricaCheck verify this lie too?\u201d <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/HesedGuru\"><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Cyprian from Brits<\/span><\/i><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> asked, leaving no doubt as to where he stood. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The attached image showed a man being arrested by Interpol officers. The accompanying text claimed that the man was HIV positive and had \u201cadded his infected blood to Cadbury products\u201d. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cIt was shown yesterday on BBC News,\u201d it added. \u201cPlease forward the message to people who you care [sic].\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<h2>Two steps to find the truth<\/h2>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The story sounds far-fetched\u2026 but that\u2019s never stopped Africa Check from sorting fact from fiction before. (See: <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/africacheck.org\/reports\/nope-nkandlas-mermaids-are-actually-from-hollywood\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Dead mermaids<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> in a president\u2019s swimming pool.) \u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Here are the two steps we took to check if the story was true.<\/span><\/p>\n<h3>1. Google the story<\/h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">We googled \u201c<\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.google.co.za\/search?q=hiv+blood+cadbury+chocolate&amp;oq=hiv+blood+cadbury+chocolate&amp;aqs=chrome..69i57.454j0j7&amp;sourceid=chrome&amp;ie=UTF-8\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">hiv blood cadbury chocolate<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201d, which quickly confirmed that this story was a hoax. \u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-16037 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/africacheck.org\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/03\/Snopes.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"589\" height=\"135\" srcset=\"https:\/\/africacheck.org\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/03\/Snopes.png 589w, https:\/\/africacheck.org\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/03\/Snopes-300x69.png 300w, https:\/\/africacheck.org\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/03\/Snopes-304x70.png 304w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 589px) 100vw, 589px\" \/>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cClaiming that various companies\u2019 food products have somehow become contaminated with HIV\/AIDS has been a prevalent form of hoax for many years, targeting foodstuffs from pineapples to canned goods to soft drinks,\u201d fellow fact-checking website <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.snopes.com\/cadbury-hiv-arrest\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Snopes explained<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This claim relating to confectionery company, Cadbury, started appearing in 2018. It is a reworked hoax, having previously <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.snopes.com\/food\/tainted\/pepsihiv.asp\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">targeted Pepsi cold drinks<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cNo warnings have been issued, nor any arrests made, in conjunction with a supposed HIV contamination of Cadbury products,\u201d reported Snopes. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It\u2019s also important to remember that HIV can not survive outside the human body for long. The virus cannot be passed on in this way.\u00a0 \u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<h3>2. Trace the image<\/h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The story turned out to be a hoax but where is the image from? We uploaded the image to <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.tineye.com\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Tineye.com<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> to try trace the image back to its original source. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It picked up that the image was published with a story on Nigerian website <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/webcache.googleusercontent.com\/search?q=cache:GiZUW-KwNfIJ:https:\/\/www.naija.ng\/69745.html+&amp;cd=1&amp;hl=en&amp;ct=clnk&amp;gl=za\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Naija.com<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> 3 years ago. It actually shows Aminu Ogwuche being extradited to Nigeria from South Sudan. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Ogwuche was accused of masterminding the <\/span><a href=\"http:\/\/studies.aljazeera.net\/en\/reports\/2014\/04\/20144299643486571.html\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">14 April 2014 bombing<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> of a bus park in Nyanya, a suburb of Nigerian capital <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.google.co.za\/maps\/place\/Abuja,+Nigeria\/data=!4m2!3m1!1s0x104e745f4cd62fd9:0x53bd17b4a20ea12b?sa=X&amp;ved=0ahUKEwihuozaj8vZAhWFI8AKHTo_C1YQ8gEI1gEwEQ\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Abuja<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The blast killed 71 people and injured 124 people.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Read our guide for more tips on <\/span><a href=\"http:\/\/bit.ly\/2nu8CAX\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">verifying images<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> on your smartphone. <em>&#8211; 01\/03\/2018<\/em><\/span><\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n"},{"title":"Ramaphosa right about \u2018big difference\u2019 between black &#038; white unemployment in SA","permalink":"https:\/\/africacheck.org\/spot-check\/ramaphosa-right-about-big-difference-between-black-white-unemployment-in-sa\/","content":"<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Replying to the <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/africacheck.org\/reports\/verifying-key-claims-in-the-2018-state-of-the-nation-debate\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">debate on his State of the Nation address<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, South Africa\u2019s newly-minted president Cyril Ramaphosa said that concerns about white people being excluded from opportunities musn\u2019t be ignored or \u201cjust willy-nilly\u201d dismissed.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">He was referring to <\/span><a href=\"http:\/\/www.vfplus.org.za\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Freedom Front Plus<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> leader Pieter Groenewald<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> who claimed that \u201cbecause of affirmative action and broad-based black economic empowerment, white young people are excluded from jobs, bursaries and opportunities based on the colour of their skin.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cWe must engage with [the concerns] and we must address them,\u201d Ramaphosa continued. \u201cAnd as we address them we should be mindful that\u2026 that statement is not borne out by reality.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cUnemployment among Africans stands at 30% and just under 7% for white people. Big difference,\u201d he <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/youtu.be\/2XuRFmNK4k0?t=1275\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">said<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Statistics South Africa\u2019s latest employment data is for October to December 2017. During that quarter, the unemployment rate at the national level was estimated at <\/span><a href=\"http:\/\/www.statssa.gov.za\/publications\/P0211\/P02114thQuarter2017.pdf#page=26\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">26.7%<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Ramaphosa is correct with regards to the difference between the narrow unemployment rate for black and white South Africans. An estimated 30% of the black workforce was unemployed, but actively looking for a job, compared to just 6.7% of the white workforce. <\/span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8211; Kate Wilkinson (20\/02\/2018)<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n<table>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Population group<\/b><\/td>\n<td><b>Narrow unemployment rate <\/b><\/td>\n<td><b>Broad unemployment rate<\/b><\/td>\n<\/tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Black <\/span><\/td>\n<td><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">30.0%<\/span><\/td>\n<td><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">40.7%<\/span><\/td>\n<\/tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Coloured <\/span><\/td>\n<td><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">23.5%<\/span><\/td>\n<td><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">29.1%<\/span><\/td>\n<\/tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Indian <\/span><\/td>\n<td><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">9.2%<\/span><\/td>\n<td><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">14.9%<\/span><\/td>\n<\/tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">White <\/span><\/td>\n<td><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">6.7%<\/span><\/td>\n<td><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">8.5%<\/span><\/td>\n<\/tr>\n<\/tbody>\n<\/table>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Source: <\/span><a href=\"http:\/\/www.statssa.gov.za\/publications\/P0211\/P02114thQuarter2017.pdf#page=26\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Statistics South Africa (Q4 2017)<\/span><\/a><\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"text-decoration: underline;\"><strong>Additional reading<\/strong><\/span>:<\/p>\n<div class=\"video-container\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"cC3RG1Eb9G\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/africacheck.org\/reports\/state-of-the-nation-address-1-president-cyril-ramaphosas-claims-weighed-up\/\">Fact-checked: Pres Cyril Ramaphosa&#8217;s first-ever State of the Nation Address<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" src=\"https:\/\/africacheck.org\/reports\/state-of-the-nation-address-1-president-cyril-ramaphosas-claims-weighed-up\/embed\/#?secret=cC3RG1Eb9G\" data-secret=\"cC3RG1Eb9G\" width=\"474\" height=\"267\" title=\"&#8220;Fact-checked: Pres Cyril Ramaphosa&#8217;s first-ever State of the Nation Address&#8221; &#8212; Africa Check\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<div class=\"video-container\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"bpgug6Kmxp\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/africacheck.org\/reports\/verifying-key-claims-in-the-2018-state-of-the-nation-debate\/\">Verifying key claims in SA&#8217;s 2018 State of the Nation address debate<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; 					<a href="https://africacheck.org/reports/nigerias-unemployment-rate-18-8-widely-tweeted/">Is Nigeria&#8217;s unemployment rate 18.8%, as widely tweeted? </a>
				</h2>

At least seven people were killed and dozens injured. Photo: AFP" />
										<p class='excerpt'>Employment figures are an important measure of a country's economic health. Were people right to question the unemployment rate for Nigeria in a widely-shared tweet? <span class="researched_by">Researched by David Ajikobi</span></p>

				<section id="from-the-blog" class="lead panel page-block from-the-blog">
		<h1 class="block-title">
		<a href="/blog">From the blog</a>
		<a href="feed://africacheck.org/feed/?post_type=reports" class="rss">RSS</a>
		<!-- 		<a href="/blog" class="read_all">Read all posts</a> -->

		</h1>
				<article>
		<h2>

<p>Is Africa Rising? Journalists and politicians debate the question. But what do they know?</p>
<p>The independent research project <a href="http://www.afrobarometer.org/">Afrobarometer</a> polled the views of more than 51,000 Africans from 34 countries from 2011-2013 and has released its findings. "32% say their personal living conditions have improved in the past year; 33% say conditions have gotten worse; 34% saw no change".</p>
<p>Check this and <a href="http://afrobarometer.org/files/documents/policy_brief/ab_r5_policybriefno1.pdf">their wider findings</a>.</p>

				<div class="row">

					<div class="col-sm-8 we-hold-public-figures-accountable">
						<!-- make a dynamic sidebar block -->
	
	<h2>We hold public figures accountable</h2>
<p><a href="http://www.poynter.org/fact-checkers-code-of-principles/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><img class="alignright size-thumbnail wp-image-10711" src="/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/ifcn-fact-checkers-code-of-principles-signatory-150x150.png" alt="ifcn-fact-checkers-code-of-principles-signatory" width="150" height="150" /></a>For democracy to function, public figures need to be held to account for what they say. The claims they make need to be checked, openly and impartially. Africa Check is an independent, non-partisan organisation which assesses claims made in the public arena using journalistic skills and evidence drawn from the latest online tools, readers, public sources and experts, sorting fact from fiction and publishing the results.</p>
		
												<nav class="about-navigation" role="navigation" aria-label="Footer Navigation">

<script id="tmpl-nf-field-wrap" type="text/template">
	<div id="nf-field-{{{ data.id }}}-wrap" class="{{{ data.renderWrapClass() }}}" data-field-id="{{{ data.id }}}">
		<#
		/*
		 * This is our main field template. It's called for every field type.
		 * Note that must have ONE top-level, wrapping element. i.e. a div/span/etc that wraps all of the template.
		 *
		 * <div>
		 * 	 <div>
		 *   	Cool Stuff
		 * 	 </div>
		 *   <span>
		 * 		Hello World!
		 *   </span>
		 * </div>
		 *
		 * is OK.
		 *
		 * <div>
		 * 		Cool Stuff
		 * </div>
		 * <span>
		 * 		Hello World!
		 * </span>
		 *
		 * is NOT ok because each of those items is on the top-level.
		 */
        #>
		<#
		/*
		 * Render our label.
		 */
        #>
		{{{ data.renderLabel() }}}
		<#
		/*
		 * Render our field element. Uses the template for the field being rendered.
		 */
        #>
		<div class="nf-field-element">{{{ data.renderElement() }}}</div>
		<#
		/*
		 * Render our Description Text.
		 */
        #>
		{{{ data.renderDescText() }}}
	</div>
</script>
